<td><a href="/wiki/St._Petronius" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petronius">St. Petronius</a></td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row">Saint day</th>
<td>4 October</td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedtoprow">
<th scope="row">Website</th>
<td><span class="official-website"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.comune.bologna.it/">Official website</a></span></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Bologna</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">j</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i>bə-<b>LOHN</b>-yə</i></small></a>; <small>Italian pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Italian" title="Help:IPA/Italian">[boˈloɲːa]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:It-Bologna.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/It-Bologna.ogg" class="internal" title="It-Bologna.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Emilian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Emilian language">Emilian</a>: <span lang="egl" xml:lang="egl"><i>Bulåggna</i></span>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[buˈlʌɲːa]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Bŏnṓnĭa</i></span>) is the capital and largest city of the <a href="/wiki/Emilia-Romagna" title="Emilia-Romagna">Emilia-Romagna</a> Region in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Italy" title="Northern Italy">Northern Italy</a>. It is the seventh most populous city in Italy, located in the heart of a <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_City_of_Bologna" title="Metropolitan City of Bologna">metropolitan area</a> (officially recognised by the Italian government as a <i><a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_cities_of_Italy" title="Metropolitan cities of Italy">città metropolitana</a></i>) of about one million.</p>
<p>The first settlements date back to at least 1000 BC. The city has been an urban centre, first under the <a href="/wiki/Etruscans" class="mw-redirect" title="Etruscans">Etruscans</a> (Velzna/Felsina) and the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> (<i>Bona</i>), then under the Romans (<i>Bononia</i>), then again in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, as a free municipality (for one century it was the fifth largest European city based on population). Home to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_universities_in_continuous_operation" title="List of oldest universities in continuous operation">oldest university in the world</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hunt_Janin_2008_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunt_Janin_2008-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ridder-Symoens_1992_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ridder-Symoens_1992-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">University of Bologna</a>, founded in 1088, Bologna hosts thousands of students who enrich the social and cultural life of the city. Famous for its towers and lengthy <a href="/wiki/Portico" title="Portico">porticoes</a>, Bologna has a well-preserved historical centre (one of the largest in Italy) thanks to a careful restoration and conservation policy which began at the end of the 1970s, on the heels of serious damage done by the urban demolition at the end of the 19th century as well as that caused by wars.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>An important cultural and artistic centre, its importance in terms of landmarks can be attributed to a varied mixture of monuments and architectural examples (medieval towers, antique buildings, churches, the layout of its historical centre) as well as works of art which are the result of a first class architectural and artistic history.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Bologna is also an important transportation crossroad for the roads and trains of Northern Italy, where many important mechanical, electronic and nutritional industries have their headquarters. According to the most recent data gathered by the European Regional Economic Growth Index (E-REGI) of 2009, Bologna is the first Italian city and the 47th European city in terms of its economic growth rate.<sup id="cite_ref-citymayors.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citymayors.com-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bologna is home to numerous prestigious cultural, economic and political institutions as well as one of the most impressive trade fair districts in Europe. In 2000 it was declared <a href="/wiki/European_capital_of_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="European capital of culture">European capital of culture</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and in 2006, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> "city of music". The city of Bologna was selected to participate in the Universal Exposition of Shanghai 2010 together with 45 other cities from around the world. Bologna is also one of the wealthiest cities in Italy, often ranking as one of the top cities in terms of quality of life in the country: in 2011 it ranked 1st out of 107 Italian cities.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Bologna" title="Timeline of Bologna">Timeline of Bologna</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG/220px-Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG/330px-Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG/440px-Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1963" data-file-height="1354" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna._Porta_Maggiore._Strada_Magiore._Torre_degli_Asinelli_IMG_3874.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Porta Maggiore, one of the twelve medieval city gates of Bologna.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Communal_fight_in_Bologna_(Sercambi).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Communal_fight_in_Bologna_%28Sercambi%29.jpg/220px-Communal_fight_in_Bologna_%28Sercambi%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Communal_fight_in_Bologna_%28Sercambi%29.jpg/330px-Communal_fight_in_Bologna_%28Sercambi%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Communal_fight_in_Bologna_%28Sercambi%29.jpg/440px-Communal_fight_in_Bologna_%28Sercambi%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Communal_fight_in_Bologna_(Sercambi).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Depiction of a 14th-century fight between the militias of the Guelf and Ghibelline factions in Bologna, from the <i>Croniche</i> of Giovanni Sercambi of Lucca.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After a long decline, Bologna was reborn in the 5th century under Bishop <a href="/wiki/St._Petronius" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petronius">Petronius</a>. According to legend, St. Petronius built the church of S. Stefano. After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of Rome">fall of Rome</a>, Bologna was a frontier stronghold of the <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Ravenna" title="Exarchate of Ravenna">Exarchate of Ravenna</a> in the Po plain, and was defended by a line of walls which did not enclose most of the ancient ruined Roman city. In 728, the city was captured by the <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombard</a> king <a href="/wiki/Liutprand,_King_of_the_Lombards" title="Liutprand, King of the Lombards">Liutprand</a>, becoming part of the Lombard Kingdom. The Germanic conquerors formed a district called "addizione longobarda" near the complex of S. Stefano. <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> stayed in this district in 786.</p>
<p>In the 11th century, under the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, Bologna began to aspire to being a free <a href="/wiki/Commune" title="Commune">commune</a>, which it was able to do when <a href="/wiki/Matilda_of_Tuscany" title="Matilda of Tuscany">Matilda of Tuscany</a> died, in 1115, and the following year the city obtained many judicial and economic concessions from Emperor <a href="/wiki/Henry_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Henry V, Holy Roman Emperor">Henry V</a>. Bologna joined the <a href="/wiki/Lombard_League" title="Lombard League">Lombard League</a> against <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Barbarossa" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick Barbarossa">Frederick Barbarossa</a> in 1164 which ended with the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Constance" title="Peace of Constance">Peace of Constance</a> in 1183; after which, the city began to expand rapidly (this is the period in which its famous towers were built) and it became one of the main commercial trade centres thanks to a system of canals that allowed large ships to come and go.</p>
<p>Traditionally said to be founded in 1088, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">University of Bologna</a> is widely considered to be the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_universities_in_continuous_operation" title="List of oldest universities in continuous operation">first university</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hunt_Janin_2008_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunt_Janin_2008-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ridder-Symoens_1992_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ridder-Symoens_1992-7">[7]</a></sup> The university originated as an international centre of study of <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Roman_law" title="Medieval Roman law">medieval Roman law</a> under major <a href="/wiki/Glossator" title="Glossator">glossators</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Irnerius" title="Irnerius">Irnerius</a>. It numbered <a href="/wiki/Dante" class="mw-redirect" title="Dante">Dante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boccaccio" class="mw-redirect" title="Boccaccio">Boccaccio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petrarch" title="Petrarch">Petrarca</a> among its students.<sup id="cite_ref-unibo_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unibo-13">[13]</a></sup> The medical school is especially famous.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 12th century, the city's families engaged in continual internecine fighting.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern">Early modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg/220px-Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg/330px-Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg/440px-Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1013" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mappa_di_Bologna_del_Blaeu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bologna in 1640.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_porte.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Bologna_porte.svg/220px-Bologna_porte.svg.png" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Bologna_porte.svg/330px-Bologna_porte.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Bologna_porte.svg/440px-Bologna_porte.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="602" data-file-height="496" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_porte.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Walls and gates of Bologna.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Troops of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">Pope Julius II</a> besieged Bologna and sacked the artistic treasures of his palace. From that point on, until the 18th century, Bologna was part of the <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a>, ruled by a cardinal legato and by a Senate which every two months elected a gonfaloniere (judge), assisted by eight elder consuls. In 1530, in front of <a href="/wiki/San_Petronio_Basilica" title="San Petronio Basilica">Saint Petronio Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> was crowned Holy Roman Emperor by Pope <a href="/wiki/Clement_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Clement VII">Clement VII</a>.</p>
<p>Then a plague at the end of the 16th century reduced the population from 72,000 to 59,000, and another in 1630 to 47,000. The population later recovered to a stable 60,000–65,000. However, there was also great progress during this era: in 1564, the Piazza del Nettuno and the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_dei_Banchi" title="Palazzo dei Banchi">Palazzo dei Banchi</a> were built, along with the <a href="/wiki/Archiginnasio" class="mw-redirect" title="Archiginnasio">Archiginnasio</a>, the centre of the University. The period of Papal rule saw the construction of many churches and other religious establishments, and the reincarnation of older ones. At this time, Bologna had ninety-six convents, more than any other Italian city. Artists working during this period in Bologna established the <a href="/wiki/Bolognese_School" title="Bolognese School">Bolognese School</a> which includes <a href="/wiki/Annibale_Carracci" title="Annibale Carracci">Annibale Carracci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domenichino" title="Domenichino">Domenichino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guercino" title="Guercino">Guercino</a> and others of European fame.<sup id="cite_ref-Raimond_Van_Marle_1924_pp_394-481_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raimond_Van_Marle_1924_pp_394-481-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_modern_and_contemporary">Late modern and contemporary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Late modern and contemporary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg/220px-Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg/330px-Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg/440px-Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2488" data-file-height="1633" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_Piazza_Maggiore_c1855.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Piazza del Nettuno in 1855, looking towards Piazza Maggiore.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1796 <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> conquered Bologna, making it the capital of the short lived <a href="/wiki/Cispadane_Republic" title="Cispadane Republic">Cispadane Republic</a>. After the fall of Napoleon, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> of 1815 placed Bologna once again under the sovereignty of the <a href="/wiki/Papal_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Papal State">Papal States</a>, leading to the uprisings of 1831 and 1848, when the Austrian garrisons which controlled the city were temporarily expelled. Eventually, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_War_of_Italian_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Second War of Italian Independence">Second War of Italian Independence</a>, on 11 and 12 March 1860 the city voted in favour of annexation by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Kingdom of Sardinia</a>, soon to become the new <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bologna suffered extensive damage during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The strategic importance of the city as industrial and railway hub connecting northern and central Italy made it a strategic target for the Allied forces. On 16 July 1943 a massive aerial bombardment destroyed much of the historic city centre and killed scores of people. The main railway station and adjoining areas were severely hit, and 44% of the buildings in the centre were listed as having been destroyed or severely damaged. The city was heavily bombed again on 25 September. The raids, which this time were not confined to the city centre, left 936 people dead and thousands injured.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the war, the city became a key centre of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_resistance_movement" title="Italian resistance movement">Italian resistance movement</a>. On 7 November 1944, a pitched battle around <a href="/wiki/Porta_Lame,_Bologna" class="mw-redirect" title="Porta Lame, Bologna">Porta Lame</a>, waged by partisans of the 7th Brigade of the <i>Gruppi d'Azione Patriottica</i> against <a href="/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic" title="Italian Social Republic">Fascist</a> and Nazi occupation forces, did not succeed in triggering a general uprising, despite being one of the largest resistance-led urban conflicts in the European theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Resistance forces entered Bologna on the morning of 21 April 1945. By this time, the Germans had already largely left the city in the face of the Allied advance, spearheaded by Polish forces advancing from the east during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bologna" title="Battle of Bologna">Battle of Bologna</a> which had been fought since 9 April. First to arrive in the centre was the 87th Infantry Regiment of the Friuli Combat Group under general <a href="/w/index.php?title=Arturo_Scattini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Arturo Scattini (page does not exist)">Arturo Scattini</a>, who entered the centre from <i>Porta Maggiore</i> to the south. Since the soldiers were dressed in British outfits, they were initially thought to be part of the allied forces; when the local inhabitants heard the soldiers were speaking Italian, they poured out on to the streets to celebrate.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_years">Post-war years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-war years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stragedibologna-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Stragedibologna-2.jpg/220px-Stragedibologna-2.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Stragedibologna-2.jpg/330px-Stragedibologna-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Stragedibologna-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="262" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stragedibologna-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aftermath of the 1980 terrorist bombing.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the post-war years, Bologna became a thriving industrial centre as well as a political stronghold of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party" title="Italian Communist Party">Italian Communist Party</a>. Between 1945 and 1999, the city had an uninterrupted series of left-wing <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Bologna#Democratic_Mayors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mayors of Bologna">mayors</a>, the first of whom was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Giuseppe_Dozza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Giuseppe Dozza (page does not exist)">Giuseppe Dozza</a>.</p>
<p>In 1977 Bologna was the scene of <a href="/wiki/Movement_of_1977#The_riots" title="Movement of 1977">rioting</a> linked to the <a href="/wiki/Movement_of_1977" title="Movement of 1977">Movement of 1977</a>, a spontaneous political movement of the time. The alleged police shooting of a <a href="/wiki/Far-left" class="mw-redirect" title="Far-left">far-left</a> activist, <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Lorusso" title="Francesco Lorusso">Francesco Lorusso</a>, sparked two days of street clashes. On 2 August 1980, at the height of the "<a href="/wiki/Years_of_Lead_(Italy)" title="Years of Lead (Italy)">years of lead</a>", a terrorist bomb was set off in the central railway station of Bologna killing 85 people and wounding 200, an event which is known in Italy as the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_massacre" title="Bologna massacre">Bologna massacre</a>. In 1995, members of the <a href="/wiki/Neo-fascist" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-fascist">neo-fascist</a> group <a href="/wiki/Nuclei_Armati_Rivoluzionari" title="Nuclei Armati Rivoluzionari">Nuclei Armati Rivoluzionari</a> were convicted for carrying out the attack, while <a href="/wiki/Licio_Gelli" title="Licio Gelli">Licio Gelli</a>—Grand Master of the underground Freemason lodge <a href="/wiki/Propaganda_Due" title="Propaganda Due">Propaganda Due (P2)</a>—was convicted for hampering the investigation, together with three agents of the secret military intelligence service <a href="/wiki/SISMI" title="SISMI">SISMI</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Pazienza" title="Francesco Pazienza">Francesco Pazienza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Musumeci" title="Pietro Musumeci">Pietro Musumeci</a>). Commemorations take place in Bologna on 2 August each year, culminating in a concert in the main square.</p>
<p>In 1999 the long tradition of left-wing mayors was interrupted by the victory of the independent candidate Giorgio Guazzaloca, who led a centre-right coalition; this brief experience ended in 2004 when <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Cofferati" title="Sergio Cofferati">Sergio Cofferati</a>, a former trade union leader, was elected. The next centre-left mayor, <a href="/wiki/Flavio_Delbono" title="Flavio Delbono">Flavio Delbono</a>, elected in June 2009, resigned in January 2010 after being involved in a corruption scandal. After a 15-month period in which the city was administered under <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Cancellieri" class="mw-redirect" title="Anna Maria Cancellieri">Anna Maria Cancellieri</a> (as a state-appointed <a href="/wiki/Prefect#Modern_sub-national_administration" title="Prefect">prefect</a>), <a href="/wiki/Virginio_Merola" title="Virginio Merola">Virginio Merola</a> was elected as mayor, leading a left-wing coalition comprising the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="Democratic Party (Italy)">Democratic Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Left_Ecology_Freedom" title="Left Ecology Freedom">Left Ecology Freedom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy_of_Values" title="Italy of Values">Italy of Values</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territory">Territory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Territory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_Bologna_01_(RaBoe).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Luftbild_Bologna_01_%28RaBoe%29.jpg/220px-Luftbild_Bologna_01_%28RaBoe%29.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Luftbild_Bologna_01_%28RaBoe%29.jpg/330px-Luftbild_Bologna_01_%28RaBoe%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Luftbild_Bologna_01_%28RaBoe%29.jpg/440px-Luftbild_Bologna_01_%28RaBoe%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="653" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_Bologna_01_(RaBoe).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial photograph of Bologna (from East to West).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bologna is situated on the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Po_Valley" title="Po Valley">Po Plain</a> at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">Apennine Mountains</a>, at the meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Reno_(river)" title="Reno (river)">Reno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savena" title="Savena">Savena</a> river valleys. As Bologna's two main watercourses flow directly to the sea, the town lies outside of the drainage basin of the <a href="/wiki/Po_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Po river">River Po</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bologna_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna (province)">Province of Bologna</a> stretches from the western edge of the Po Plain on the border with <a href="/wiki/Ferrara" title="Ferrara">Ferrara</a> to the Tuscan-Emilian Apennines. The centre of the town is 54 metres (177&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> (while elevation within the municipality ranges from 29 metres (95&#160;ft) in the suburb of Corticella to 300 metres (980&#160;ft) in Sabbiuno and the Colle della Guardia). The Province of Bologna stretches from the Po Plain into the Apennines; the highest point in the province is the peak of Corno alle Scale (in <a href="/wiki/Lizzano_in_Belvedere" title="Lizzano in Belvedere">Lizzano in Belvedere</a>) at 1,945 metres (6,381&#160;ft) above sea level.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bologna has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: Cfa, <a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha</a>: Do).</p>
<p>Annual precipitation oscillates between around 450&#160;mm (18&#160;in) and 900&#160;mm (35&#160;in),<sup id="cite_ref-stat_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat-20">[20]</a></sup> with the majority generally falling in spring and autumn. <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">Snow</a> occasionally falls during winter and heavy snowfalls; the last major event was in <a href="/wiki/Early_2012_European_cold_wave" title="Early 2012 European cold wave">February 2012</a>, when almost a meter of snow fell in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg/220px-Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg/330px-Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg/440px-Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_-_Palazzo_d%27Accursio_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_5-3-2005_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Palazzo D'Accursio, Bologna's City Hall.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The legislative body of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_communes" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian communes">municipality</a> is the City Council (<i>Consiglio Comunale</i>), which is composed of 36 councillors elected every five years with a proportional system, contextually to the mayoral elections. The executive body is the City Committee (<i>Giunta Comunale</i>), composed by 7 <a href="/wiki/Assessor_(Italy)" title="Assessor (Italy)">assessors</a>, that is nominated and presieded over by a directly elected <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Bologna" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mayors of Bologna">Mayor</a>. The current mayor of Bologna is <a href="/wiki/Virginio_Merola" title="Virginio Merola">Virginio Merola</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="Democratic Party (Italy)">PD</a>), elected on 16 May 2011 with the 50.5% of the votes.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The municipality of Bologna was subdivided into nine administrative Boroughs (<i>Quartieri</i>) until 2015. Each Borough is governed by a Council (<i>Consiglio</i>) and a President, elected contextually to the city Mayor. The urban organization is governed by the Italian Constitution (art. 114). The Boroughs have the power to advise the Mayor with nonbinding opinions on a large spectrum of topics (environment, construction, public health, local markets) and exercise the functions delegated to them by the City Council; in addition they are supplied with an autonomous founding in order to finance local activities. Of the nine boroughs, eight were governed by the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="Democratic Party (Italy)">Democratic Party</a> and one by the <a href="/wiki/Lega_Nord" title="Lega Nord">Lega Nord</a>. In July 2015 has been approved a reform to reduce the Boroughs from nine to six, as a result of the spending review to save up to 200.000 euros.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna,_Santuario_della_Madonna_di_San_Luca_004.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_the_Madonna_di_San_Luca,_Bologna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanctuary of the Madonna di San Luca, Bologna">Sanctuary of the Madonna di San Luca</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Until the late 19th century, when a large-scale urban renewal project was undertaken, Bologna remained one of the few remaining large walled cities in Europe; to this day and despite having suffered considerable bombing damage in 1944, Bologna's 350 acres (141.64&#160;ha) historic centre is Europe's second largest,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> containing an immense wealth of important medieval, renaissance, and baroque artistic monuments.</p>
<p>Bologna developed along the Via Emilia as an Etruscan and later Roman colony; the Via Emilia still runs straight through the city under the changing names of Strada Maggiore, Rizzoli, Ugo Bassi, and San Felice. Due to its Roman heritage, the central streets of Bologna, today largely pedestrianized, follow the grid pattern of the Roman settlement. The original Roman ramparts were supplanted by a high medieval system of fortifications, remains of which are still visible, and finally by a third and final set of ramparts built in the 13th century, of which numerous sections survive. No more than twenty medieval defensive towers remain out of up to 180 that were built in the 12th and 13th centuries before the arrival of unified civic government. The most famous of the <a href="/wiki/Towers_of_Bologna" title="Towers of Bologna">towers of Bologna</a> are the central "Due Torri" (<i>Asinelli</i> and <i>Garisenda</i>), whose iconic leaning forms provide a popular symbol of the town.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The cityscape is further enriched by its elegant and extensive porticoes, for which the city is famous. In total, there are some 38 kilometres (24 miles) of <a href="/wiki/Portico" title="Portico">porticoes</a> in the city's historical centre<sup id="cite_ref-unesco_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-28">[28]</a></sup> (over 45&#160;km (28&#160;mi) in the city proper), which make it possible to walk for long distances sheltered from the elements.</p>
<p>The Portico di San Luca is possibly the world's longest.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> It connects <a href="/wiki/Porta_Saragozza" class="mw-redirect" title="Porta Saragozza">Porta Saragozza</a> (one of the twelve gates of the ancient walls built in the Middle Ages, which circled a 7.5&#160;km (4.7&#160;mi) part of the city) with the <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_the_Madonna_di_San_Luca,_Bologna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanctuary of the Madonna di San Luca, Bologna">Sanctuary of the Madonna di San Luca</a>, a church begun in 1723 on the site of an 11th-century edifice which had already been enlarged in the 14th century, prominently located on a hill (289 metres (948 feet)) overlooking the town, which is one of Bologna's main landmarks. The winding 666 vault arcade, almost four kilometres (3,796&#160;m or 12,454&#160;ft) long, effectively links San Luca, as the church is commonly called, to the centre of town. Its porticos provide shelter for the traditional procession which every year since 1433 has carried a Byzantine icon of the Madonna with Child attributed to <a href="/wiki/Luke_the_Evangelist" title="Luke the Evangelist">Luke the Evangelist</a> down to the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Cathedral" title="Bologna Cathedral">Bologna Cathedral</a> during Ascension week.<sup id="cite_ref-unesco_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other churches in Bologna include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Basilica of <a href="/wiki/San_Petronio_Basilica" title="San Petronio Basilica">San Petronio</a>, one of the world's largest churches</li>
<li>Basilica of <a href="/wiki/Santo_Stefano,_Bologna" title="Santo Stefano, Bologna">Santo Stefano</a> and sanctuary</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Domenico" title="Basilica of San Domenico">Basilica of San Domenico</a> and sanctuary</li>
<li>Basilica of <a href="/wiki/San_Francesco_(Bologna)" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francesco (Bologna)">St Francis</a></li>
<li>Basilica of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_dei_Servi" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Maria dei Servi">Santa Maria dei Servi</a></li>
<li>Basilica of <a href="/wiki/San_Giacomo_Maggiore_(Bologna)" class="mw-redirect" title="San Giacomo Maggiore (Bologna)">San Giacomo Maggiore</a> (13th–14th century), featuring Renaissance artworks such as the <a href="/wiki/Pala_Bentivoglio" class="mw-redirect" title="Pala Bentivoglio">Bentivoglio Altarpiece</a> by <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Costa_the_Elder" class="mw-redirect" title="Lorenzo Costa the Elder">Lorenzo Costa</a></li>
<li>Church of <a href="/wiki/San_Michele_in_Bosco" title="San Michele in Bosco">San Michele in Bosco</a></li>
</ul>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Bologna_Panorama.jpg/700px-Bologna_Panorama.jpg" width="700" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Bologna_Panorama.jpg/1050px-Bologna_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Bologna_Panorama.jpg/1400px-Bologna_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11750" data-file-height="5514" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bologna_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View from the top of the Basilica di San Petronio. In center the dome of Santuario di Santa Maria della Vita, right – "Due Torri": Asinelli (higher) and Garisenda.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unipol_Tower_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Unipol_Tower_2.JPG/170px-Unipol_Tower_2.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Unipol_Tower_2.JPG/255px-Unipol_Tower_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Unipol_Tower_2.JPG/340px-Unipol_Tower_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unipol_Tower_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Unipol_Tower" title="Unipol Tower">Unipol Tower</a>, at 127&#160;m, is the city's tallest building.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bologna is an important railway and motorway hub in Italy. The economy of Bologna is characterized by a flourishing industrial sector, traditionally based on the transformation of agricultural and zootechnical products (<a href="/wiki/Granarolo" class="mw-redirect" title="Granarolo">Granarolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Segafredo_Zanetti" class="mw-redirect" title="Segafredo Zanetti">Segafredo Zanetti</a>). It also includes machinery (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Coesia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coesia (page does not exist)">Coesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/IMA_(company)" title="IMA (company)">IMA</a>), energy (<a href="/wiki/Hera_Group" title="Hera Group">Hera Group</a>), automotive (<a href="/wiki/Ducati" title="Ducati">Ducati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamborghini" title="Lamborghini">Lamborghini</a>), footwear, textile, engineering, chemical, printing and publishing industries, as well as a strong financial, insurance (<a href="/wiki/Unipol" title="Unipol">Unipol</a>) and retail (<a href="/wiki/Coop_Italia" class="mw-redirect" title="Coop Italia">Coop Italia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conad" title="Conad">Conad</a>) activity.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg/170px-Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg" width="170" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg/255px-Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg/340px-Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2248" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiera_District_Towers_BO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fiera District</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city's Fiera District (exhibition centre) is one of the largest in Europe, with important yearly international expos focused on the automobile sector (<a href="/wiki/Bologna_Motor_Show" title="Bologna Motor Show">Bologna Motor Show</a>), ceramics for the building industry (International Exhibition of Ceramic Tiles and Bathroom Furnishings) and food industry. In addition, several important firms in the fields of food, tobacco and electronics have their headquarters in the urban area of Bologna, as well as important retail and wholesale trade (the "Centergross" in <a href="/wiki/Argelato" title="Argelato">Argelato</a>, esabilished in 1973), and one of the largest Italian food processing companies (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Conserve_Italia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Conserve Italia (page does not exist)">Conserve Italia</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bologna is home to the <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Guglielmo Marconi International Airport">Guglielmo Marconi International Airport</a>, recently<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> expanded to accommodate larger aircraft. Today, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">seventh</a> busiest Italian airport for passenger traffic (7 million passengers handled in 2016). <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Centrale_railway_station" title="Bologna Centrale railway station">Bologna Centrale railway station</a> is one of the most important train hubs in Italy thanks to the city's strategic location. It serves 58 million passengers annually.<sup id="cite_ref-gs1_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gs1-31">[31]</a></sup> In addition, Bologna San Donato <a href="/wiki/Classification_yard" title="Classification yard">classification yard</a>, with 33 railway tracks, is the largest in Italy by size and traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The city is also served by a large network of public bus lines, including <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Bologna" title="Trolleybuses in Bologna">trolleybus lines</a>, operated since 2012 by Trasporto Passeggeri Emilia-Romagna SpA (TPER).</p>
<p>A large <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter rail</a> service is currently under development (see <a href="/wiki/Bologna_metropolitan_railway_service" title="Bologna metropolitan railway service">Bologna metropolitan railway service</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bologna_Public_Transportation_Statistics">Bologna Public Transportation Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Bologna Public Transportation Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Bologna, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 53 min. 9% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 12 min, while 16% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 5.4 km, while 7% travel for over 12 km in a single direction. <sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At the end of 2016, the city proper had a population of 388,254 (while 1 million live in the greater Bologna area), located in the province of Bologna, <a href="/wiki/Emilia_Romagna" class="mw-redirect" title="Emilia Romagna">Emilia Romagna</a>, of whom 46.7% were male and 53.3% were female. Minors (children ages 18 and younger) totalled 12.86 percent of the population compared to pensioners who number 27.02 percent. This compares with the Italian average of 18.06 percent (minors) and 19.94 percent (pensioners). The average age of Bologna resident is 51 compared to the Italian average of 42. In the five years between 2002 and 2007, the population of Bologna grew by 0.0 percent, while Italy as a whole grew by 3.56 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The current birth rate of Bologna is 8.07 births per 1,000 inhabitants compared to the Italian average of 9.45 births.</p>
<p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 89.47% of the population was <a href="/wiki/Italian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian people">Italian</a>. The largest immigrant group came from other European countries (mostly <a href="/wiki/Romanians_in_Italy" title="Romanians in Italy">Romanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>): 2.82%, <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Italy" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipinos in Italy">Filipino</a>): 1.50%, and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> (mostly from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>): 1.39%.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Archiginnasio,_Bologna,_Italy,_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/The_Archiginnasio%2C_Bologna%2C_Italy%2C_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG/220px-The_Archiginnasio%2C_Bologna%2C_Italy%2C_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/The_Archiginnasio%2C_Bologna%2C_Italy%2C_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG/330px-The_Archiginnasio%2C_Bologna%2C_Italy%2C_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/The_Archiginnasio%2C_Bologna%2C_Italy%2C_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG/440px-The_Archiginnasio%2C_Bologna%2C_Italy%2C_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Archiginnasio,_Bologna,_Italy,_the_wing_with_the_Anatomical_theatre.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Courtyard of the 16th-century <a href="/wiki/Archiginnasio_of_Bologna" title="Archiginnasio of Bologna">Archiginnasio</a>, historical seat of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">University of Bologna</a>—Europe's oldest, founded in 1088.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">University of Bologna</a>, founded in 1088, is the oldest university in the world, and was an important centre of European intellectual life during the Middle Ages, attracting scholars from Italy and throughout Europe. A unique heritage of medieval art, exemplified by the illuminated manuscripts and jurists' tombs produced in the city from the 13th to the 15th centuries, provides a cultural backdrop to the renown of the medieval institution. The Studium, as it was originally known, began as a loosely organized teaching system with each master collecting fees from students on an individual basis. The location of the early University was thus spread throughout the city, with various colleges being founded to support students of a specific nationality.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg/220px-Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg/330px-Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg/440px-Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Archiginnasio-teatroanatomico.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Anatomical_theatre_of_the_Archiginnasio" title="Anatomical theatre of the Archiginnasio">Anatomical theatre of the Archiginnasio</a>, dating from 1637.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Napoleonic era, the headquarters of the university were moved to their present location on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Via_Zamboni&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Via Zamboni (page does not exist)">Via Zamboni</a> (formerly Via San Donato), in the north-eastern sector of the city centre. Today, the University's 11 schools, 33 departments, and 93 libraries are spread across the city and include four subsidiary campuses in nearby <a href="/wiki/Cesena" title="Cesena">Cesena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forl%C3%AC" title="Forlì">Forlì</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">Ravenna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a>. Noteworthy students present at the university in centuries past included <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petrarch" title="Petrarch">Petrarch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Becket" title="Thomas Becket">Thomas Becket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Nicholas_V" title="Pope Nicholas V">Pope Nicholas V</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_of_Rotterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="Erasmus of Rotterdam">Erasmus of Rotterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Martyr_Vermigli" title="Peter Martyr Vermigli">Peter Martyr Vermigli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Copernicus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bassi" title="Laura Bassi">Laura Bassi</a>, appointed in 1732, became the first woman to officially teach at a college in Europe. In more recent history, <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Galvani" title="Luigi Galvani">Luigi Galvani</a>, the discoverer of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Biological_electricity&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Biological electricity (page does not exist)">biological electricity</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi" title="Guglielmo Marconi">Guglielmo Marconi</a>, the pioneer of radio technology, also worked at the University. The University of Bologna remains one of the most respected and dynamic post-secondary educational institutions in Italy. To this day, Bologna is still very much a university town, and the city's population swells from 400,000 to over 500,000 whenever classes are in session. This community includes a great number of Erasmus, Socrates, and overseas students.</p>
<p>The university's <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Orto_Botanico_dell%27Universit%C3%A0_di_Bologna" title="Orto Botanico dell'Università di Bologna">Orto Botanico dell'Università di Bologna</a>, was established in 1568; it is the fourth oldest in Europe.</p>
<p>Bologna is also home to other universities such as the <a href="/wiki/The_Johns_Hopkins_University_SAIS_Bologna_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="The Johns Hopkins University SAIS Bologna Center">Bologna Center</a> of <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> School of Advanced International Studies (SAIS). SAIS Bologna was founded in 1955 as the first campus of a US post-graduate school to open in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> It was inspired by Marshall Plan efforts to build a cultural bridge between America and Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Today, the Bologna Center also hosts the <i>Associazione italo-americana "Luciano Finelli,"</i> which supports cross-cultural awareness and exchange between Italy and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the city are present several <a href="/wiki/High_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="High schools">high schools</a> and institutes superiors, both public and <a href="/wiki/Independent_school" title="Independent school">independent schools</a>.</p>
<p>The secondary schools are:</p>
<ul>
<li>High School of Art and Design Francesco Arcangeli</li>
<li>Liceo ginnasio statale (<a href="/wiki/Liceo_scientifico" title="Liceo scientifico">Liceo scientifico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liceo_Classico" class="mw-redirect" title="Liceo Classico">Liceo Classico</a>) <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Galvani" title="Luigi Galvani">Luigi Galvani</a></li>
<li>Liceo ginnasio statale (<a href="/wiki/Liceo_Classico" class="mw-redirect" title="Liceo Classico">Liceo Classico</a>) <a href="/wiki/Marco_Minghetti" title="Marco Minghetti">Marco Minghetti</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Liceo_scientifico" title="Liceo scientifico">Liceo scientifico</a> <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Fermi" title="Enrico Fermi">Enrico Fermi</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liceo_scientifico" title="Liceo scientifico">Liceo scientifico</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Niccol%C3%B2_Copernico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Niccolò Copernico (page does not exist)">Niccolò Copernico</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Liceo_scientifico" title="Liceo scientifico">Liceo scientifico</a> <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Mattei" title="Enrico Mattei">Enrico Mattei</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Independent_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent School">Independent School</a> are:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museomusicabosala7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Museomusicabosala7.jpg/220px-Museomusicabosala7.jpg" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Museomusicabosala7.jpg/330px-Museomusicabosala7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Museomusicabosala7.jpg/440px-Museomusicabosala7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="1722" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Museomusicabosala7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/International_museum_and_library_of_music" class="mw-redirect" title="International museum and library of music">International museum and library of music</a> displays ancient musical instruments and unique musical scores from the 16th to the 20th centuries.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over the centuries, Bologna has acquired many nicknames: "the learned one" (<i>la dotta</i>) is a reference to its university; "the fat one" (<i>la grassa</i>) refers to its cuisine.</p>
<p>"The red one" (<i>la rossa</i>) originally refers to the colour of the roofs in the historic centre, but this nickname is also connected to the political situation in the city, started after World War II: until the election of a centre-right mayor in 1999, the city was renowned as a bastion of <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a> in particular the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party" title="Italian Communist Party">Italian Communist Party</a>. The centre-left regained power again in the 2004 mayoral elections, with the election of <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Cofferati" title="Sergio Cofferati">Sergio Cofferati</a>. It was one of the first European cities to experiment with the concept of <a href="/wiki/Free_public_transport" title="Free public transport">free public transport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city of Bologna was appointed a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> City of Music on 26 May 2006. According to UNESCO, "As the first Italian city to be appointed to the Network, Bologna has demonstrated a rich musical tradition that is continuing to evolve as a vibrant factor of contemporary life and creation. It has also shown a strong commitment to promoting music as an important vehicle for inclusion in the fight against racism and in an effort to encourage economic and social development. Fostering a wide range of genres from classical to electronic, jazz, folk and opera, Bologna offers its citizens a musical vitality that deeply infiltrates the city's professional, academic, social and cultural facets."<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_and_performing_arts">Entertainment and performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Entertainment and performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arena_del_Sole.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Arena_del_Sole.jpg/220px-Arena_del_Sole.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Arena_del_Sole.jpg/330px-Arena_del_Sole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Arena_del_Sole.jpg/440px-Arena_del_Sole.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arena_del_Sole.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Façade of "Arena del Sole" theatre.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">theatre</a> was a popular form of entertainment in Bologna until the 16th century. The first public theater was the Teatro alla Scala, active since 1547 in <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_del_Podest%C3%A0_(Bologna)" class="mw-redirect" title="Palazzo del Podestà (Bologna)">Palazzo del Podestà</a>.</p>
<p>An important figure of Italian Bolognese theatre was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alfredo_Testoni&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alfredo Testoni (page does not exist)">Alfredo Testoni</a>, the playwright, author of <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Cardinal_Lambertini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Cardinal Lambertini (page does not exist)">The Cardinal Lambertini</a></i>, which has had great theatrical success since 1905, repeated on screen by the Bolognese actor <a href="/wiki/Gino_Cervi" title="Gino Cervi">Gino Cervi</a>.</p>
<p>In 1998, the City of Bologna initiated the project "Bologna dei Teatri" (Bologna of the Theatres), an association of the major theatrical facilities in the city. This is a circuit of theatres which offer diverse and colourful cultural and theatrical opportunities, ranging from Bolognese dialect to contemporary <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dance</a>, but with a communications strategy and promoting unity. Specifically, the shows on the bill in various theatres participating in the project are advertised weekly through a single poster.</p>
<p>Bologna's opera house is the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Comunale_di_Bologna" title="Teatro Comunale di Bologna">Teatro Comunale di Bologna</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Orchestra_Mozart" title="Orchestra Mozart">Orchestra Mozart</a>, whose music director was <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Abbado" title="Claudio Abbado">Claudio Abbado</a> until his death in 2014, was created in 2004.</p>
<p>Bologna hosts a number of festivals and other events, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Angelica: International Contemporary Music Festival <sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>Bologna Contemporanea: international festival on contemporary <sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>Bolognafestival: international classical music festival <sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>Bologna Jazz Festival: the Italian autumn jazz event <sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li>Biografilm Festival: International Film Festival devote to Biography <sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>BilBolBul:International Comic Festival <sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>Danza Urbana: International Street Contemporary Dance Festival <sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/F.I.S.Co." title="F.I.S.Co.">F.I.S.Co</a>: International Festival on Contemporary art (now merged in <a href="/wiki/Live_Arts_Week" title="Live Arts Week">Live Arts Week</a>)</li>
<li>Future Film Festival: International Festival on animation and special effects<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li>Il Cinema Ritrovato: International Film Festival about Forgotten Films <sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Live_Arts_Week" title="Live Arts Week">Live Arts Week</a></li>
<li>Gender Bender: International Festival on the gender identity, sexual orientation and body representation <sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>Homework festival: electronic music festival<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li>Human Rights Film Festival <sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Netmage" title="Netmage">Netmage</a>: International Festival dedicated to Electronic Art (now merged in <a href="/wiki/Live_Arts_Week" title="Live Arts Week">Live Arts Week</a>)</li>
<li>Some Prefer cake: Italian lesbian film festival <sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zecchino_d%27Oro" title="Zecchino d'Oro">Zecchino d'Oro</a>: International festival of children's song</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg/220px-Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg/330px-Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg/440px-Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1864" data-file-height="1360" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tagliatelle_al_ragu_Bolognese.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Tagliatelle" title="Tagliatelle">Tagliatelle</a> al ragù Bolognese</i> as served in Bologna.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bologna is renowned for its culinary tradition. It has given its name to the well-known <a href="/wiki/Bolognese_sauce" title="Bolognese sauce">Bolognese sauce</a>, a meat based pasta sauce called in Italy <i><a href="/wiki/Rag%C3%B9" title="Ragù">ragù</a> alla bolognese</i> but in the city itself just <i>ragù</i> as in <i><a href="/wiki/Tagliatelle" title="Tagliatelle">Tagliatelle</a> al ragù</i>. Situated in the fertile Po River Valley, the rich local cuisine depends heavily on meats and cheeses. As in all of Emilia-Romagna, the production of cured <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> meats such as <a href="/wiki/Prosciutto" title="Prosciutto">prosciutto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mortadella" title="Mortadella">mortadella</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salumi" title="Salumi">salumi</a> is an important part of the local food industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Well-regarded nearby vineyards include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pignoletto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pignoletto (page does not exist)">Pignoletto</a> dei Colli Bolognesi, <a href="/wiki/Lambrusco" title="Lambrusco">Lambrusco</a> di Modena and <a href="/wiki/Sangiovese" title="Sangiovese">Sangiovese</a> di Romagna.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Tagliatelle" title="Tagliatelle">Tagliatelle</a> with <a href="/wiki/Rag%C3%B9" title="Ragù">ragù</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lasagne" title="Lasagne">lasagne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tortellini" title="Tortellini">tortellini</a> served in broth, and mortadella, the original <a href="/wiki/Bologna_sausage" title="Bologna sausage">Bologna sausage</a>, are among the local specialties.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Traditional Bolognese desserts are often linked to holidays, such as fave dei morti, multi-coloured almond paste cookies made for <a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day" title="All Saints' Day">All Saints' Day</a>, jam-filled raviole cookies that are served on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph's Day">Saint Joseph's Day</a>, and carnival sweets known as sfrappole, a light and delicate fried pastry topped with powder sugar. Torta di riso, a custard-like cake made of almonds, rice and amaretto, is made throughout the year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg/300px-Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg" width="300" height="73" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg/450px-Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg/600px-Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4628" data-file-height="1131" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prepartita_bologna_bari.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 38,000-capacity <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Renato_Dall%27Ara" title="Stadio Renato Dall'Ara">Stadio Renato Dall'Ara</a> is the home of <a href="/wiki/Bologna_FC_1909" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna FC 1909">Bologna FC 1909</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A sporting nickname for Bologna is <i>Basket City</i> in reference to the successes of the town's two rival historic <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> clubs, <a href="/wiki/Fortitudo_Pallacanestro_Bologna" title="Fortitudo Pallacanestro Bologna">Fortitudo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virtus_Pallacanestro_Bologna" title="Virtus Pallacanestro Bologna">Virtus</a>, though the clubs are now often referred to by the names of their current sponsors.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff2003_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff2003-54">[54]</a></sup> Of the two, the latter won 15 <a href="/wiki/Lega_Basket_Serie_A" title="Lega Basket Serie A">Italian basketball championships</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Euroleague" class="mw-redirect" title="Euroleague">Euroleagues</a> making them one of the most influential European basketball clubs; the former won two league titles between 1999 and 2005. The rivalry is temporarily dormant since Fortitudo left the country's professional ranks when, following the <a href="/wiki/Lega_Basket_Serie_A_2008%E2%80%9309" class="mw-redirect" title="Lega Basket Serie A 2008–09">2008–09 season</a>, the club was relegated from the top-level <a href="/wiki/Lega_Basket_Serie_A" title="Lega Basket Serie A">Lega A</a> to <a href="/wiki/LegADue" class="mw-redirect" title="LegADue">LegADue</a>, before being relegated further to the nominally amateur Serie A Dilettanti for financial reasons; in the 2012–13 season, <a href="/wiki/Fortitudo_Bologna" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortitudo Bologna">Fortitudo</a> will play in the <a href="/wiki/LegADue" class="mw-redirect" title="LegADue">LegADue</a>. The Italian Basketball League, which operates both Lega A and LegADue, has its headquarters in Bologna.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Association Football">Football</a> also has a strong tradition in Bologna. The city's main club, <a href="/wiki/Bologna_F.C._1909" title="Bologna F.C. 1909">Bologna F.C. 1909</a>, have won seven Italian league championships (the latest in <a href="/wiki/1963-64_Serie_A" class="mw-redirect" title="1963-64 Serie A">1963–64</a>), which make them the sixth most successful team in the history of the league; in their heyday in the 1930s Bologna FC were called <i>"Lo squadrone che tremare il mondo fa"</i> (Italian for "The Team that Shakes the World"). The club play at the 38,000-capacity <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Renato_Dall%27Ara" title="Stadio Renato Dall'Ara">Stadio Renato Dall'Ara</a>, which has hosted the Italian national team in both football and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino national football team</a>. It was also a venue at the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cup</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is also present in the city: Rugby Bologna 1928 is not only one of the oldest Italian rugby union clubs but also the first ever club affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/Federazione_Italiana_Rugby" class="mw-redirect" title="Federazione Italiana Rugby">Italian rugby union federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and, to date (2014) is Italy's oldest rugby union club still in operation. The club took part to the top tier of the Italian championship for the first 25 years of their history never winning the title but getting to the runner-up place several times; they returned in top division (Serie A1 then Super 10), in the late 1990s and faced serious financial problems which led them to the relegation and almost to disappearance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bologna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
